New York City announced in 2013 it planned to spend between $10 and $20 billion on local flood protection, reduction of the heat island effect with reflective and green roofs, flood-hardening of hospitals and public housing, resiliency in food supply, and beach enhancement; rezoned to allow private property owners to move critical features to upper stories; and required electrical utilities to harden infrastructure against flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>  Study of a large <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor_Storm-Surge_Barrier" title="New York Harbor Storm-Surge Barrier">storm barrier</a> spanning the entire harbor was previously proposed by the Governor of New York, but was dismissed in the City's plans.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, the German Federal Cabinet adopted the 'German Strategy for Adaptation to Climate Change'<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> that sets out a framework for adaptation in Germany. Priorities are to collaborate with the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">Federal States</a> of Germany in assessing the risks of climate change, identifying action areas and defining appropriate goals and measures. In 2011, the Federal Cabinet adopted the 'Adaptation Action Plan'<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> that is accompanied by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://climate-adapt.eea.europa.eu/countries-regions/countries/germany">other items</a> such as research programs, adaptation assessments and systematic observations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2018, the New York WILD film festival gave the "Best Short Film" award to a 12-minute documentary, titled <i>Adaptation Bangladesh: Sea Level Rise</i>. The film explores the way in which Bangladeshi farmers are preventing their farms from flooding by building floating gardens made of water hyacinth and bamboo.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Ice_Stupa" title="Ice Stupa">ice stupa</a> designed by <a href="/wiki/Sonam_Wangchuk_(engineer)#Ice_Stupa" title="Sonam Wangchuk (engineer)">Sonam Wangchuk</a> brings glacial water to farmers in the Himalayan Desert of Ladakh, India.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Mesoamerica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Mesoamerica today, climate change is one of the main threats to rural central american farmers, as the region is plagued with frequent droughts, cyclones and the El Niño- Southern-Oscillation.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Although there is a wide variety of adaption strategies, these can vary dramatically from country to country. Many of the adjustments that have been made are primarily agricultural or related to water supply. Some of these adaptive strategies include restoration of degraded lands, rearrangement of land uses across territories, livelihood diversification, changes to sowing dates or water harvest, and even migration.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The lack of available resources in Mesoamerica continues to pose as a barrier to more substantial adaptations, so the changes made today are much more incremental.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nepal">Nepal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Nepal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation_in_Nepal" title="Climate change adaptation in Nepal">Climate change adaptation in Nepal</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_adaptation">Opposition to adaptation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Opposition to adaptation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, writing in 1992 in <i><a href="/wiki/Earth_in_the_Balance" title="Earth in the Balance">Earth in the Balance</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-GoreEB239,240_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoreEB239,240-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> adaptation represented a "kind of laziness, an arrogant faith in our ability to react in time to save our skins".<sup id="cite_ref-NatureTaboo_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatureTaboo-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Climate commentator David Roberts has written that "(b)oth mitigation and adaption are necessary at this point. But for every day mitigation is delayed, the need for adaptation grows," which is problematic because "adaptation is more expensive and requires bigger government than mitigation."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_adaptation_denial">Climate adaptation denial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Climate adaptation denial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to a <a href="/wiki/Report" title="Report">report</a><sup id="cite_ref-GreenPeace_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreenPeace-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> released by Greenpeace USA in September 2013, climate change denial and the campaigns designed to block adaptation measures grew mainly out of the 1990s negotiations slated to develop a global agreement.  During these talks, a number of lobby groups were established with an objective of developing doubt within policymakers and the media through the use of publications in the guise of true science.  This tactic, similar to those of large tobacco companies, was utilized by the lobby groups in the hopes of delaying action and blurring the lines between the valid scientific efforts to challenge climate change findings and those designed to merely undermine the credibility of the scientific community.  This strategy feeds into the "uncertainty argument" and develops an impression of debate through references to the uncertainty of scientific findings that exist in any research model.  Additional tactics that the lobbyist groups have used include releasing non-stories manufactured from stolen emails and communications plans to develop more media coverage of the uncertainty argument.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict-sensitive_adaptation">Conflict-sensitive adaptation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Conflict-sensitive adaptation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A book by the Berliner Wissenschafts-Verlag on 'conflict-sensitive adaptation' sheds light on unintended damaging effects of climate adaptation measures.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> For example, when disadvantaged groups are left out of the planning process, adaptation methods such as agricultural or water programmes may increase vulnerabilities. The book draws on findings from Africa and outlines how conflict-sensitive adaptation activities should look that are cognizant of the conflict-effects adaptation may have. The authors provide a "Memorandum for Action on Adaptation for Peace and Stability" that outlines principles to support processes for adaptation and peace such as the establishment of peace and conflict assessments for adaptation programmes, mainstreaming climate change adaptation in conflict-prone contexts, applying conflict sensitive approaches or provisions to ensure participatory processes to design and implement adaptation measures.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relevant_IPCC_reports">Relevant IPCC reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Relevant IPCC reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC)</a> produced two separate reports: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.grida.no/climate/ipcc_tar/wg3/004.htm">Climate Change 2001: Mitigation</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060710143740/http://www.grida.no/climate/ipcc_tar/wg2/006.htm">Climate Change 2001: Impacts, Adaptation and Vulnerability</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relevant_United_States_sources">Relevant United States sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Relevant United States sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.usgcrp.gov/usgcrp/default.php">US Global Change Research Program</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.usgcrp.gov/usgcrp/Library/nationalassessment/foundation.htm">US National Assessment—Preparing for a Changing Climate report</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ncgia.ucsb.edu/pubs/CA_Report.pdf">California Regional Assessment: Preparing for Climate Change: The Potential Consequences of Climate Variability and Change for California</a> (not on Federal site) 2002</li>
<li>The US <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Technology_Assessment" title="Office of Technology Assessment">Office of Technology Assessment</a> (OTA) published two reports containing detailed assessments of mitigation and adaptation strategies
<ul><li>"Changing by Degrees" investigates options for controlling emissions of carbon dioxide, the most troublesome anthropogenic greenhouse gas (OTA 1991).</li>
<li>"Preparing for an Uncertain Climate" examines how managed natural resource systems—such as water, agriculture, and forests—might adapt to changing environmental conditions brought about by global warming (OTA 1993).</li></ul></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120215160910/http://www.georgetownclimate.org/adaptation/clearinghouse">Adaptation Clearinghouse of the Georgetown Climate Center</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_government_sources">Other government sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other government sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several countries have taken a lead in climate vulnerability assessment and adaptation planning. Their web sites contain reports, strategies, and tools which other countries can customize to their own situation.
</p>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ukcip.org.uk/">The United Kingdom's Climate Impacts Programme</a> (UKCIP)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20071012070304/http://www.greenhouse.gov.au/impacts/">Australia</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090204153036/http://adaptation.nrcan.gc.ca/index_e.php">Canada</a></li>
<li>The Canadian National Assessment: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090213075012/http://adaptation.nrcan.gc.ca/assess/2007/index_e.php">From Impacts to Adaptation: Canada in a Changing Climate 2007</a> discusses current and future risks and opportunities that climate change presents to Canada, with a focus on human and managed systems.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_relevant_sources">Other relevant sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_adaptation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Other relevant sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to government and United Nations reports, an extensive research literature assesses options for response to global warming. Much of this literature addresses the potential economic costs associated with different strategies.
</p>
<ul><li>The World Bank has worked with developing countries to support adaptation planning since 1999. It has also analyzed how to mainstream adaptation planning into its loan and grant programs. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.worldbank.org/WBSITE/EXTERNAL/TOPICS/ENVIRONMENT/EXTCC/0,,contentMDK:20484574%7EmenuPK:1172760%7EpagePK:148956%7EpiPK:216618%7EtheSitePK:407864,00.html">This page has publications to download</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> has a series of studies on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.adb.org/publications/economics-climate-change-east-asia">Economics of Climate Change</a> in the Asia-Pacific region. The studies provide cost analysis of both adaptation and mitigation measures.</li>
<li>Indigo Development has a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.indigodev.com/climadaptlinks.html">page of links to government and research web sites on climate adaptation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> has issued a report detailing the need for high emissions countries to support adaptation in developing countries: Adapting to climate change, What's needed in poor countries, and who should pay Oxfam Briefing Paper 104</li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eldis.org/go/topics">Eldis platform</a>, run by the Institute of Development Studies at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sussex" title="University of Sussex">University of Sussex</a> has literature on adaptation and sustainable development</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/WEAP" title="WEAP">WEAP</a> (Water Evaluation And Planning system) assists water resources researchers and planners in assessing impacts of and adaptations to climate change.</li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.weadapt.org/">weADAPT platform</a> encourages the collaborative development of tools for adaptation and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wikiadapt.org/">sharing experiences from adaptation projects</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a> runs the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.adaptationlearning.net/">adaptation learning mechanism</a> which provides country case studies of adaptation.</li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20111230064904/http://cecar.unu.edu/">UN-CECAR</a> research and development of courses on climate change and adaptation</li>
<li>The UNFCCC has a database on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20081114101033/http://maindb.unfccc.int/public/adaptation/">local adaptation measures</a> and information on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120218231656/http://unfccc.int/adaptation/items/4159.phpadaptation">the international climate negotiations</a></li>
<li>"Economic Approaches to Greenhouse Warming" provides a summary of Yale economist <a href="/wiki/William_Nordhaus" title="William Nordhaus">William Nordhaus</a>' ideas (1991). Nordhaus questions the motivation for countries to pursue relatively costly measures for responding to global warming given current scientific uncertainty about the problem's magnitude and estimates potential economic impacts may not be that high, particularly for <a href="/wiki/Developed_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed economies">developed economies</a>.</li>
<li>Economist <a href="/wiki/William_R._Cline" title="William R. Cline">William R. Cline</a> offers an opposing view, arguing potential economic costs of unabated global warming could be very high. In the monograph, "Global Warming: The Economic Stakes", Cline (1992) assesses the potential cost of damages from global warming and the cost of efforts to control greenhouse gas emissions.</li>
<li>"Coping with Global Climate Change: The Role of Adaptation in the United States" <a href="/wiki/Pew_Center_on_Global_Climate_Change" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Center on Global Climate Change">Pew Center on Global Climate Change</a>, June 2004.</li>
<li>National Center for Policy Analysis  <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20050914181308/http://www.ncpa.org/pub/st/st278/">"Living with Global Warming"</a>.
